## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / ordinary differential equations)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics modeled by rate-law ODEs. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are concentration-dependent rate laws (reaction order, saturation/inhibition, autocatalysis) and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing or decay of activity.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion, e.g., surface-limited or high-substrate regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like kinetics, simple degradation)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or dimerization-limited depletion)
- Nth-order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (effective reaction order / empirical kinetics)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady-state concentration c1)
- Linear production minus first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant source with linear sink; chemostat-like balance)
- Autocatalytic (logistic-type) growth with carrying concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplifying formation limited by depletion/capacity)
- Saturating loss (Monod-like in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to limited catalyst/active sites)
- Substrate inhibition / bell-shaped dependence: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1 + c2 * A**2) (rate decreases at very high A due to inhibition or deactivation)
- Time-dependent deactivation of rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective first-order with catalyst/activity decay in time)
- Periodic/forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally driven conditions modulating rate, e.g., light/dose cycling)
- Mixed-order with background drift: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (lumped approximation of multiple parallel pathways over a narrow range)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production sign: negative dA_dt terms indicate depletion; positive terms indicate net formation or influx.
- Reaction order identification: linear in A suggests first-order; quadratic in A suggests bimolecular/self-interaction; A**c implies effective fractional/complex order.
- Equilibrium/steady state: appearance of (A - c) implies relaxation toward an equilibrium concentration c; stability depends on the sign of the coefficient.
- Parallel pathways: sums like (-c0*A - c1*A**2) indicate concurrent first- and second-order loss channels dominating in different concentration regimes.
- Capacity limitation: factors like (c - A) multiplying A imply self-limited growth/production as A approaches a maximum (resource or site limitation).
- Catalyst/site limitation: rational forms A/(A + c) imply saturation of rate at high A (limited active sites or finite catalytic capacity).
- Inhibition/deactivation at high A: denominators with additional + c*A**2 (or similar) produce a peak rate at intermediate A and reduced rate at very high A.
- Non-autonomous kinetics: explicit dependence on t (e.g., exp(-c*t), sin(c*t), polynomials in t) suggests changing conditions, aging/deactivation, or external forcing.

GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_z*A**c4/(c5*A**c6 + c7)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
f(t,A)=\frac{0.8260241661931926\,A^2}{0.8635828411814722\,A^4+1}\;-\;0.10132643987768028\,A\;-\;0.10132643987768028\,A\,e^{-0.07564103214721236\,t}.
\]
Key structural facts:
- Exactly two \(t\)-dependent pieces: one is \(A e^{kt}\) with \(k=-0.07564...\); the rational term is \(t\)-independent.
- The only non-polynomial-in-\(A\) part is the rational \(A^2/(1+\alpha A^4)\). No logs, cos, Abs, sqrt, etc.
- Denominator is \(1+\alpha A^4\) (constant term 1, plus \(A^4\) term). No \(A^0\) scaling freedom inside the denominator except via \(\alpha\).

Now check candidates.

1) Has multiple terms over \((A^4+c2)\) plus a log term \(c7 e^{c8 t}\log(c9|A|+1)\). GT has no log; cannot remove unless \(c7=0\). Even then, remaining \(t\)-dependence is \(e^{c1 t}\) multiplying both \(A^5\) and \(A\) over same denominator; GT’s exponential term is \(-0.1013 A e^{kt}\) with no denominator. Cannot match for all \(A\). No.

2) Similar to (1) but extra \(A^{c7}c8 e^{c9 t}\). To match GT must kill that term (set \(c8=0\) or similar), but still has exponential terms divided by \((A^4+c2)\) unlike GT. No.

3) All terms are over \((A^4+c1)\) including exponentials; GT has linear-in-\(A\) terms not divided by a rational denominator. No.

4) Uses \((A^{c0}+c3)\) denominators and mixes powers; exponential terms also divided by that denominator. GT’s exponential term is not divided by any \(A\)-dependent denominator. No.

5) Same issue: everything is over \((A^{c0}+c2)\); GT has standalone \(-0.1013A\) and \(-0.1013A e^{kt}\). No.
